uid="ZKghfg" prefix="r6" component-url="/_astro/PostCopyButton.-PGtk4At.js" component-export="default" renderer-url="/_astro/client.DGA1VMK9.js" props="{&quot;title&quot;:[0,&quot;How to Structure Vue Projects&quot;],&quot;content&quot;:[0,&quot;import Aside from \&quot;@features/mdx-components/components/Aside.astro\&quot;;\nimport FileTree from \&quot;@features/filetree/components/FileTree.astro\&quot;;\n\n## Quick Summary\n\nThis post covers specific Vue project structures suited for different project sizes:\n\n- Flat structure for small projects\n- Atomic Design for scalable applications\n- Modular approach for larger projects\n- Feature Sliced Design for complex applications\n- Micro frontends for enterprise-level solutions\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n## Introduction\n\nWhen starting a Vue project, one of the most critical decisions you&#39;ll make is how to structure it. The right structure enhances scalability, maintainability, and collaboration within your team. This consideration aligns with **Conway&#39;s Law**:\n\n&gt; \&quot;Organizations which design systems are constrained to produce designs which are copies of the communication structures of these organizations.\&quot;  \n&gt; — Mel Conway\n\nIn essence, your Vue application&#39;s architecture will reflect your organization&#39;s structure, influencing how you should plan your project&#39;s layout.\n\n![Diagram of Conway&#39;s Law](../../assets/images/how-to-structure-vue/conway.png)\n\nWhether you&#39;re building a small app or an enterprise-level solution, this guide covers specific project structures suited to different scales and complexities.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Flat Structure: Perfect for Small Projects\n\nAre you working on a small-scale Vue project or a proof of concept? A simple, flat folder structure might be the best choice to keep things straightforward and avoid unnecessary complexity.\n\n&lt;FileTree\n  tree={[\n    {\n      name: \&quot;src\&quot;,\n      open: true,\n      children: [\n        {\n          name: \&quot;components\&quot;,\n          children: [\n            { name: \&quot;BaseButton.vue\&quot; },\n            { name: \&quot;BaseCard.vue\&quot; },\n            { name: \&quot;PokemonList.vue\&quot; },\n            { name: \&quot;PokemonCard.vue\&quot; },\n          ],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;composables\&quot;,\n          children: [{ name: \&quot;usePokemon.js\&quot; }],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;utils\&quot;,\n          children: [{ name: \&quot;validators.js\&quot; }],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;layout\&quot;,\n          children: [\n            { name: \&quot;DefaultLayout.vue\&quot; },\n            { name: \&quot;AdminLayout.vue\&quot; },\n          ],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;plugins\&quot;,\n          children: [{ name: \&quot;translate.js\&quot; }],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;views\&quot;,\n          children: [{ name: \&quot;Home.vue\&quot; }, { name: \&quot;PokemonDetail.vue\&quot; }],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;router\&quot;,\n          children: [{ name: \&quot;index.js\&quot; }],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;store\&quot;,\n          children: [{ name: \&quot;index.js\&quot; }],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;assets\&quot;,\n          children: [\n            { name: \&quot;images\&quot;, children: [] },\n            { name: \&quot;styles\&quot;, children: [] },\n          ],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;tests\&quot;,\n          children: [{ name: \&quot;...\&quot;, comment: \&quot;test files\&quot; }],\n        },\n        { name: \&quot;App.vue\&quot; },\n        { name: \&quot;main.js\&quot; },\n      ],\n    },\n  ]}\n/&gt;\n\n### Pros and Cons\n\n&lt;div class=\&quot;overflow-x-auto\&quot;&gt;\n  &lt;table class=\&quot;custom-table\&quot;&gt;\n    &lt;thead&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;th&gt;✅ Pros&lt;/th&gt;\n        &lt;th&gt;❌ Cons&lt;/th&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n    &lt;/thead&gt;\n    &lt;tbody&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Easy to implement&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Not scalable&lt;/td&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Minimal setup&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Becomes cluttered as the project grows&lt;/td&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Ideal for small teams or solo developers&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Lack of clear separation of concerns&lt;/td&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n    &lt;/tbody&gt;\n  &lt;/table&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;\n\n---\n\n## 2. Atomic Design: Scalable Component Organization\n\n![Atomic Design Diagram](../../assets/images/atomic/diagram.svg)\n\nFor larger Vue applications, Atomic Design provides a clear structure. This approach organizes components into a hierarchy from simplest to most complex.\n\n### The Atomic Hierarchy\n\n- **Atoms:** Basic elements like buttons and icons.\n- **Molecules:** Groups of atoms forming simple components (e.g., search bars).\n- **Organisms:** Complex components made up of molecules and atoms (e.g., navigation bars).\n- **Templates:** Page layouts that structure organisms without real content.\n- **Pages:** Templates filled with real content to form actual pages.\n\nThis method ensures scalability and maintainability, facilitating a smooth transition between simple and complex components.\n\n&lt;FileTree\n  tree={[\n    {\n      name: \&quot;src\&quot;,\n      open: true,\n      children: [\n        {\n          name: \&quot;components\&quot;,\n          open: true,\n          children: [\n            {\n              name: \&quot;atoms\&quot;,\n              children: [{ name: \&quot;AtomButton.vue\&quot; }, { name: \&quot;AtomIcon.vue\&quot; }],\n            },\n            {\n              name: \&quot;molecules\&quot;,\n              children: [\n                { name: \&quot;MoleculeSearchInput.vue\&quot; },\n                { name: \&quot;MoleculePokemonThumbnail.vue\&quot; },\n              ],\n            },\n            {\n              name: \&quot;organisms\&quot;,\n              children: [\n                { name: \&quot;OrganismPokemonCard.vue\&quot; },\n                { name: \&quot;OrganismHeader.vue\&quot; },\n              ],\n            },\n            {\n              name: \&quot;templates\&quot;,\n              children: [\n                { name: \&quot;TemplatePokemonList.vue\&quot; },\n                { name: \&quot;TemplatePokemonDetail.vue\&quot; },\n              ],\n            },\n          ],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;pages\&quot;,\n          children: [\n            { name: \&quot;PageHome.vue\&quot; },\n            { name: \&quot;PagePokemonDetail.vue\&quot; },\n          ],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;composables\&quot;,\n          children: [{ name: \&quot;usePokemon.js\&quot; }],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;utils\&quot;,\n          children: [{ name: \&quot;validators.js\&quot; }],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;layout\&quot;,\n          children: [\n            { name: \&quot;LayoutDefault.vue\&quot; },\n            { name: \&quot;LayoutAdmin.vue\&quot; },\n          ],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;plugins\&quot;,\n          children: [{ name: \&quot;translate.js\&quot; }],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;router\&quot;,\n          children: [{ name: \&quot;index.js\&quot; }],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;store\&quot;,\n          children: [{ name: \&quot;index.js\&quot; }],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;assets\&quot;,\n          children: [\n            { name: \&quot;images\&quot;, children: [] },\n            { name: \&quot;styles\&quot;, children: [] },\n          ],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;tests\&quot;,\n          children: [{ name: \&quot;...\&quot;, comment: \&quot;test files\&quot; }],\n        },\n        { name: \&quot;App.vue\&quot; },\n        { name: \&quot;main.js\&quot; },\n      ],\n    },\n  ]}\n/&gt;\n\n### Pros and Cons\n\n&lt;div class=\&quot;overflow-x-auto\&quot;&gt;\n  &lt;table class=\&quot;custom-table\&quot;&gt;\n    &lt;thead&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;th&gt;✅ Pros&lt;/th&gt;\n        &lt;th&gt;❌ Cons&lt;/th&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n    &lt;/thead&gt;\n    &lt;tbody&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Highly scalable&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Can introduce overhead in managing layers&lt;/td&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Organized component hierarchy&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Initial complexity in setting up&lt;/td&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Reusable components&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Might be overkill for smaller projects&lt;/td&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Improves collaboration among teams&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;&lt;/td&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n    &lt;/tbody&gt;\n  &lt;/table&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;\n\n&lt;Aside type=\&quot;info\&quot; title=\&quot;Want to Learn More About Atomic Design?\&quot;&gt;\n  Check out my detailed blog post on [Atomic Design in Vue and\n  Nuxt](../atomic-design-vue-or-nuxt).\n&lt;/Aside&gt;\n\n---\n\n## 3. Modular Approach: Feature-Based Organization\n\nAs your project scales, consider a **Modular Monolithic Architecture**. This structure encapsulates each feature or domain, enhancing maintainability and preparing for potential evolution towards microservices.\n\n&lt;FileTree\n  tree={[\n    {\n      name: \&quot;src\&quot;,\n      open: true,\n      children: [\n        {\n          name: \&quot;core\&quot;,\n          open: true,\n          children: [\n            {\n              name: \&quot;components\&quot;,\n              children: [{ name: \&quot;BaseButton.vue\&quot; }, { name: \&quot;BaseIcon.vue\&quot; }],\n            },\n            { name: \&quot;models\&quot;, children: [] },\n            { name: \&quot;store\&quot;, children: [] },\n            { name: \&quot;services\&quot;, children: [] },\n            {\n              name: \&quot;views\&quot;,\n              children: [\n                { name: \&quot;DefaultLayout.vue\&quot; },\n                { name: \&quot;AdminLayout.vue\&quot; },\n              ],\n            },\n            {\n              name: \&quot;utils\&quot;,\n              children: [{ name: \&quot;validators.js\&quot; }],\n            },\n          ],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;modules\&quot;,\n          open: true,\n          children: [\n            {\n              name: \&quot;pokemon\&quot;,\n              open: true,\n              children: [\n                {\n                  name: \&quot;components\&quot;,\n                  children: [\n                    { name: \&quot;PokemonThumbnail.vue\&quot; },\n                    { name: \&quot;PokemonCard.vue\&quot; },\n                    { name: \&quot;PokemonListTemplate.vue\&quot; },\n                    { name: \&quot;PokemonDetailTemplate.vue\&quot; },\n                  ],\n                },\n                { name: \&quot;models\&quot;, children: [] },\n                {\n                  name: \&quot;store\&quot;,\n                  children: [{ name: \&quot;pokemonStore.js\&quot; }],\n                },\n                { name: \&quot;services\&quot;, children: [] },\n                {\n                  name: \&quot;views\&quot;,\n                  children: [{ name: \&quot;PokemonDetailPage.vue\&quot; }],\n                },\n                {\n                  name: \&quot;tests\&quot;,\n                  children: [{ name: \&quot;pokemonTests.spec.js\&quot; }],\n                },\n              ],\n            },\n            {\n              name: \&quot;search\&quot;,\n              open: false,\n              children: [\n                {\n                  name: \&quot;components\&quot;,\n                  children: [{ name: \&quot;SearchInput.vue\&quot; }],\n                },\n                { name: \&quot;models\&quot;, children: [] },\n                {\n                  name: \&quot;store\&quot;,\n                  children: [{ name: \&quot;searchStore.js\&quot; }],\n                },\n                { name: \&quot;services\&quot;, children: [] },\n                { name: \&quot;views\&quot;, children: [] },\n                {\n                  name: \&quot;tests\&quot;,\n                  children: [{ name: \&quot;searchTests.spec.js\&quot; }],\n                },\n              ],\n            },\n          ],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;assets\&quot;,\n          children: [\n            { name: \&quot;images\&quot;, children: [] },\n            { name: \&quot;styles\&quot;, children: [] },\n          ],\n        },\n        { name: \&quot;scss\&quot;, children: [] },\n        { name: \&quot;App.vue\&quot; },\n        { name: \&quot;main.ts\&quot; },\n        { name: \&quot;router.ts\&quot; },\n        { name: \&quot;store.ts\&quot; },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;tests\&quot;,\n          children: [{ name: \&quot;...\&quot;, comment: \&quot;test files\&quot; }],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;plugins\&quot;,\n          children: [{ name: \&quot;translate.js\&quot; }],\n        },\n      ],\n    },\n  ]}\n/&gt;\n\n### Alternative: Simplified Flat Feature Structure\n\nA common pain point in larger projects is excessive folder nesting, which can make navigation and file discovery more difficult. Here&#39;s a simplified, flat feature structure that prioritizes IDE-friendly navigation and reduces cognitive load:\n\n&lt;FileTree\n  tree={[\n    {\n      name: \&quot;features\&quot;,\n      open: true,\n      children: [\n        {\n          name: \&quot;project\&quot;,\n          open: true,\n          children: [\n            { name: \&quot;project.composable.ts\&quot; },\n            { name: \&quot;project.data.ts\&quot; },\n            { name: \&quot;project.store.ts\&quot; },\n            { name: \&quot;project.types.ts\&quot; },\n            { name: \&quot;project.utils.ts\&quot; },\n            { name: \&quot;project.utils.test.ts\&quot; },\n            { name: \&quot;ProjectList.vue\&quot; },\n            { name: \&quot;ProjectItem.vue\&quot; },\n          ],\n        },\n      ],\n    },\n  ]}\n/&gt;\n\nThis structure offers key advantages:\n\n- **Quick Navigation**: Using IDE features like \&quot;Quick Open\&quot; (Ctrl/Cmd + P), you can find any project-related file by typing \&quot;project...\&quot;\n- **Reduced Nesting**: All feature-related files are at the same level, eliminating deep folder hierarchies\n- **Clear Ownership**: Each file&#39;s name indicates its purpose\n- **Pattern Recognition**: Consistent naming makes it simple to understand each file&#39;s role\n- **Test Colocation**: Tests live right next to the code they&#39;re testing\n\n---\n\n## 4. Feature-Sliced Design: For Complex Applications\n\n**Feature-Sliced Design** is ideal for big, long-term projects. This approach breaks the application into different layers, each with a specific role.\n\n![Feature-Sliced Design Diagram](../../assets/images/how-to-structure-vue/feature-sliced.png)\n\n### Layers of Feature-Sliced Design\n\n- **App:** Global settings, styles, and providers.\n- **Processes:** Global business processes, like user authentication flows.\n- **Pages:** Full pages built using entities, features, and widgets.\n- **Widgets:** Combines entities and features into cohesive UI blocks.\n- **Features:** Handles user interactions that add value.\n- **Entities:** Represents core business models.\n- **Shared:** Reusable utilities and components unrelated to specific business logic.\n\n&lt;FileTree\n  tree={[\n    {\n      name: \&quot;src\&quot;,\n      open: true,\n      children: [\n        {\n          name: \&quot;app\&quot;,\n          open: true,\n          children: [\n            { name: \&quot;App.vue\&quot; },\n            { name: \&quot;main.js\&quot; },\n            { name: \&quot;app.scss\&quot; },\n          ],\n        },\n        { name: \&quot;processes\&quot;, children: [] },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;pages\&quot;,\n          children: [{ name: \&quot;Home.vue\&quot; }, { name: \&quot;PokemonDetailPage.vue\&quot; }],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;widgets\&quot;,\n          children: [\n            { name: \&quot;UserProfile.vue\&quot; },\n            { name: \&quot;PokemonStatsWidget.vue\&quot; },\n          ],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;features\&quot;,\n          open: true,\n          children: [\n            {\n              name: \&quot;pokemon\&quot;,\n              children: [\n                { name: \&quot;CatchPokemon.vue\&quot; },\n                { name: \&quot;PokemonList.vue\&quot; },\n              ],\n            },\n            {\n              name: \&quot;user\&quot;,\n              children: [{ name: \&quot;Login.vue\&quot; }, { name: \&quot;Register.vue\&quot; }],\n            },\n          ],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;entities\&quot;,\n          open: true,\n          children: [\n            {\n              name: \&quot;user\&quot;,\n              children: [{ name: \&quot;userService.js\&quot; }, { name: \&quot;userModel.js\&quot; }],\n            },\n            {\n              name: \&quot;pokemon\&quot;,\n              children: [\n                { name: \&quot;pokemonService.js\&quot; },\n                { name: \&quot;pokemonModel.js\&quot; },\n              ],\n            },\n          ],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;shared\&quot;,\n          open: true,\n          children: [\n            {\n              name: \&quot;ui\&quot;,\n              children: [\n                { name: \&quot;BaseButton.vue\&quot; },\n                { name: \&quot;BaseInput.vue\&quot; },\n                { name: \&quot;Loader.vue\&quot; },\n              ],\n            },\n            {\n              name: \&quot;lib\&quot;,\n              children: [{ name: \&quot;api.js\&quot; }, { name: \&quot;helpers.js\&quot; }],\n            },\n          ],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;assets\&quot;,\n          children: [\n            { name: \&quot;images\&quot;, children: [] },\n            { name: \&quot;styles\&quot;, children: [] },\n          ],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;router\&quot;,\n          children: [{ name: \&quot;index.js\&quot; }],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;store\&quot;,\n          children: [{ name: \&quot;index.js\&quot; }],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;tests\&quot;,\n          children: [{ name: \&quot;featureTests.spec.js\&quot; }],\n        },\n      ],\n    },\n  ]}\n/&gt;\n\n### Pros and Cons\n\n&lt;div class=\&quot;overflow-x-auto\&quot;&gt;\n  &lt;table class=\&quot;custom-table\&quot;&gt;\n    &lt;thead&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;th&gt;✅ Pros&lt;/th&gt;\n        &lt;th&gt;❌ Cons&lt;/th&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n    &lt;/thead&gt;\n    &lt;tbody&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;High cohesion and clear separation&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Initial complexity in understanding the layers&lt;/td&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Scalable and maintainable&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Requires thorough planning&lt;/td&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Facilitates team collaboration&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Needs consistent enforcement of conventions&lt;/td&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n    &lt;/tbody&gt;\n  &lt;/table&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;\n\n&lt;Aside type=\&quot;tip\&quot; title=\&quot;Learn More About Feature-Sliced Design\&quot;&gt;\n  Visit the [official Feature-Sliced Design\n  documentation](https://feature-sliced.design/) for an in-depth understanding.\n&lt;/Aside&gt;\n\n---\n\n## 5. Micro Frontends: Enterprise-Level Solution\n\n**Micro frontends** apply the microservices concept to frontend development. Teams can work on distinct sections of a web app independently, enabling flexible development and deployment.\n\n![Micro Frontend Diagram](../../assets/images/how-to-structure-vue/microfrontend.png)\n\n### Key Components\n\n- **Application Shell:** The main controller handling basic layout and routing, connecting all micro frontends.\n- **Decomposed UIs:** Each micro frontend focuses on a specific part of the application using its own technology stack.\n\n### Pros and Cons\n\n&lt;div class=\&quot;overflow-x-auto\&quot;&gt;\n  &lt;table class=\&quot;custom-table\&quot;&gt;\n    &lt;thead&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;th&gt;✅ Pros&lt;/th&gt;\n        &lt;th&gt;❌ Cons&lt;/th&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n    &lt;/thead&gt;\n    &lt;tbody&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Independent deployments&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;High complexity in orchestration&lt;/td&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Scalability across large teams&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Requires robust infrastructure&lt;/td&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Technology-agnostic approach&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Potential inconsistencies in user experience&lt;/td&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n    &lt;/tbody&gt;\n  &lt;/table&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;\n\n&lt;Aside type=\&quot;caution\&quot; title=\&quot;Note\&quot;&gt;\n  Micro frontends are best suited for large, complex projects with multiple\n  development teams. This approach can introduce significant complexity and is\n  usually not necessary for small to medium-sized applications.\n&lt;/Aside&gt;\n\n&lt;Aside type=\&quot;tip\&quot; title=\&quot;Deep Dive into Microfrontends\&quot;&gt;\n  Want to learn how to actually implement microfrontends with Vue? Check out my\n  comprehensive guide: [How to build Microfrontends with Module Federation and\n  Vue](../how-to-build-microfrontends-with-module-federation-and-vue) - includes\n  working code, architectural decisions, and a complete reference project.\n&lt;/Aside&gt;\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\n![Conclusion](../../assets/images/how-to-structure-vue/conclusion.png)\n\nSelecting the right project structure depends on your project&#39;s size, complexity, and team organization. The more complex your team or project is, the more you should aim for a structure that facilitates scalability and maintainability.\n\nYour project&#39;s architecture should grow with your organization, providing a solid foundation for future development.\n\n### Comparison Chart\n\n&lt;div class=\&quot;overflow-x-auto\&quot;&gt;\n  &lt;table class=\&quot;custom-table\&quot;&gt;\n    &lt;thead&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;th&gt;Approach&lt;/th&gt;\n        &lt;th&gt;Description&lt;/th&gt;\n        &lt;th&gt;✅ Pros&lt;/th&gt;\n        &lt;th&gt;❌ Cons&lt;/th&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n    &lt;/thead&gt;\n    &lt;tbody&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;\n          &lt;strong&gt;Flat Structure&lt;/strong&gt;\n        &lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Simple structure for small projects&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Easy to implement&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Not scalable, can become cluttered&lt;/td&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;\n          &lt;strong&gt;Atomic Design&lt;/strong&gt;\n        &lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Hierarchical component-based structure&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Scalable, organized, reusable components&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Overhead in managing layers, initial complexity&lt;/td&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;\n          &lt;strong&gt;Modular Approach&lt;/strong&gt;\n        &lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Feature-based modular structure&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Scalable, encapsulated features&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Potential duplication, requires discipline&lt;/td&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;\n          &lt;strong&gt;Feature-Sliced Design&lt;/strong&gt;\n        &lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Functional layers and slices for large projects&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;High cohesion, clear separation&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Initial complexity, requires thorough planning&lt;/td&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n      &lt;tr&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;\n          &lt;strong&gt;Micro Frontends&lt;/strong&gt;\n        &lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Independent deployments of frontend components&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;Independent deployments, scalable&lt;/td&gt;\n        &lt;td&gt;High complexity, requires coordination between teams&lt;/td&gt;\n      &lt;/tr&gt;\n    &lt;/tbody&gt;\n  &lt;/table&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;\n\n---\n\n## General Rules and Best Practices\n\nBefore concluding, let&#39;s highlight some general rules you can apply to every structure. These guidelines are important for maintaining consistency and readability in your codebase.\n\n### Base Component Names\n\nUse a prefix for your UI components to distinguish them from other components.\n\n**Bad:**\n\n&lt;FileTree\n  tree={[\n    {\n      name: \&quot;components\&quot;,\n      open: true,\n      children: [\n        { name: \&quot;MyButton.vue\&quot; },\n        { name: \&quot;VueTable.vue\&quot; },\n        { name: \&quot;Icon.vue\&quot; },\n      ],\n    },\n  ]}\n/&gt;\n\n**Good:**\n\n&lt;FileTree\n  tree={[\n    {\n      name: \&quot;components\&quot;,\n      open: true,\n      children: [\n        { name: \&quot;BaseButton.vue\&quot; },\n        { name: \&quot;BaseTable.vue\&quot; },\n        { name: \&quot;BaseIcon.vue\&quot; },\n      ],\n    },\n  ]}\n/&gt;\n\n### Related Component Names\n\nGroup related components together by naming them accordingly.\n\n**Bad:**\n\n&lt;FileTree\n  tree={[\n    {\n      name: \&quot;components\&quot;,\n      open: true,\n      children: [\n        { name: \&quot;TodoList.vue\&quot; },\n        { name: \&quot;TodoItem.vue\&quot; },\n        { name: \&quot;TodoButton.vue\&quot; },\n      ],\n    },\n  ]}\n/&gt;\n\n**Good:**\n\n&lt;FileTree\n  tree={[\n    {\n      name: \&quot;components\&quot;,\n      open: true,\n      children: [\n        { name: \&quot;TodoList.vue\&quot; },\n        { name: \&quot;TodoListItem.vue\&quot; },\n        { name: \&quot;TodoListItemButton.vue\&quot; },\n      ],\n    },\n  ]}\n/&gt;\n\n### Order of Words in Component Names\n\nComponent names should start with the highest-level words and end with descriptive modifiers.\n\n**Bad:**\n\n&lt;FileTree\n  tree={[\n    {\n      name: \&quot;components\&quot;,\n      open: true,\n      children: [\n        { name: \&quot;ClearSearchButton.vue\&quot; },\n        { name: \&quot;ExcludeFromSearchInput.vue\&quot; },\n        { name: \&quot;LaunchOnStartupCheckbox.vue\&quot; },\n      ],\n    },\n  ]}\n/&gt;\n\n**Good:**\n\n&lt;FileTree\n  tree={[\n    {\n      name: \&quot;components\&quot;,\n      open: true,\n      children: [\n        { name: \&quot;SearchButtonClear.vue\&quot; },\n        { name: \&quot;SearchInputExclude.vue\&quot; },\n        { name: \&quot;SettingsCheckboxLaunchOnStartup.vue\&quot; },\n      ],\n    },\n  ]}\n/&gt;\n\n### Organizing Tests\n\nDecide whether to keep your tests in a separate folder or alongside your components. Both approaches are valid, but consistency is key.\n\n#### Approach 1: Separate Test Folder\n\n&lt;FileTree\n  tree={[\n    {\n      name: \&quot;vue-project\&quot;,\n      open: true,\n      children: [\n        {\n          name: \&quot;src\&quot;,\n          open: true,\n          children: [\n            {\n              name: \&quot;components\&quot;,\n              children: [{ name: \&quot;MyComponent.vue\&quot; }],\n            },\n            {\n              name: \&quot;views\&quot;,\n              children: [{ name: \&quot;HomeView.vue\&quot; }],\n            },\n          ],\n        },\n        {\n          name: \&quot;tests\&quot;,\n          open: true,\n          children: [\n            {\n              name: \&quot;components\&quot;,\n              children: [{ name: \&quot;MyComponent.spec.js\&quot; }],\n            },\n            {\n              name: \&quot;views\&quot;,\n              children: [{ name: \&quot;HomeView.spec.js\&quot; }],\n            },\n          ],\n        },\n      ],\n    },\n  ]}\n/&gt;\n\n#### Approach 2: Inline Test Files\n\n&lt;FileTree\n  tree={[\n    {\n      name: \&quot;vue-project\&quot;,\n      open: true,\n      children: [\n        {\n          name: \&quot;src\&quot;,\n          open: true,\n          children: [\n            {\n              name: \&quot;components\&quot;,\n              open: true,\n              children: [\n                { name: \&quot;MyComponent.vue\&quot; },\n                { name: \&quot;MyComponent.spec.js\&quot; },\n              ],\n            },\n            {\n              name: \&quot;views\&quot;,\n              open: true,\n              children: [\n                { name: \&quot;HomeView.vue\&quot; },\n                { name: \&quot;HomeView.spec.js\&quot; },\n              ],\n            },\n          ],\n        },\n      ],\n    },\n  ]}\n/&gt;\n\n---\n\n## Additional Resources\n\n- [Official Vue.js Style Guide](https://vuejs.org/style-guide/)\n- [Micro Frontends - Extending Microservice Ideas to Frontend Development](https://micro-frontends.org/)\n- [Martin Fowler on Micro Frontends](https://martinfowler.com/articles/micro-frontends.html)\n- [Official Feature-Sliced Design Documentation](https://feature-sliced.design/)\n\n---&quot;]}" ssr client="load" opts="{&quot;name&quot;:&quot;PostCopyButton&quot;,&quot;value&quot;:true}" await-children><button class="focus-outline inline-flex items-center gap-1.5 rounded-md border border-skin-line bg-skin-card px-2.5 py-1.5 text-xs font-medium text-skin-base opacity-80 transition-all hover:border-skin-accent/50 hover:text-skin-accent hover:opacity-100" aria-label="Copy post as markdown" title="Copy post as markdown for AI/LLM"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" class="h-3.5 w-3.5" viewBox="0 0 20 20" fill="currentColor"><path d="M8 3a1 1 0 011-1h2a1 1 0 110 2H9a1 1 0 01-1-1z"></path><path d="M6 3a2 2 0 00-2 2v11a2 2 0 002 2h8a2 2 0 002-2V5a2 2 0 00-2-2 3 3 0 01-3 3H9a3 3 0 01-3-3z"></path></svg><span>Copy Post</span></button><!--astro:end--></astro-island> </div> <nav class="mb-8 astro-sbmhws2g" aria-labelledby="series-heading"> <div class="mb-1 text-sm font-bold tracking-wide text-skin-accent astro-sbmhws2g"> Vue Architecture Guide </div> <h2 id="series-heading" class="mb-2 text-xs font-semibold uppercase tracking-widest text-skin-accent astro-sbmhws2g">

<ul>
<li>Flat structure for small projects</li>
<li>Atomic Design for scalable applications</li>
<li>Modular approach for larger projects</li>
<li>Feature Sliced Design for complex applications</li>
<li>Micro frontends for enterprise-level solutions</li>
</ul>

<h2 id="introduction">Introduction<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#introduction"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h2>
<p>When starting a Vue project, one of the most critical decisions you’ll make is how to structure it. The right structure enhances scalability, maintainability, and collaboration within your team. This consideration aligns with <strong>Conway’s Law</strong>:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>“Organizations which design systems are constrained to produce designs which are copies of the communication structures of these organizations.”<br/>
— Mel Conway</p>
</blockquote>
<p>In essence, your Vue application’s architecture will reflect your organization’s structure, influencing how you should plan your project’s layout.</p>
<p><img src="/_astro/conway.DxSL5JXQ_Z1azlTQ.webp" alt="Diagram of Conway's Law" loading="lazy" decoding="async" fetchpriority="auto" width="1136" height="768"></p>
<p>Whether you’re building a small app or an enterprise-level solution, this guide covers specific project structures suited to different scales and complexities.</p>
<hr/>
<h2 id="1-flat-structure-perfect-for-small-projects">1. Flat Structure: Perfect for Small Projects<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#1-flat-structure-perfect-for-small-projects"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h2>
<p>Are you working on a small-scale Vue project or a proof of concept? A simple, flat folder structure might be the best choice to keep things straightforward and avoid unnecessary complexity.</p>
<nav class="file-tree astro-htwbjus4" aria-label="File tree"> <ul class="file-tree__list astro-htwbjus4"> <li class="file-tree__item astro-o25vlg2d" style="--level: 0;"> <details class="file-tree__folder astro-o25vlg2d" open> <summary class="astro-o25vlg2d"> <span class="file-tree__caret astro-o25vlg2d" aria-hidden="true">

d="M24,1.61H14.06L12,5.16,9.94,1.61H0L12,22.39ZM12,14.08,5.16,2.23H9.59L12,6.41l2.41-4.18h4.43Z" class="astro-o25vlg2d"></path> </svg>  <span class="file-tree__name astro-o25vlg2d">App.vue</span>  </ul> </details>   </li>  </ul> </nav> 
<h3 id="pros-and-cons">Pros and Cons<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#pros-and-cons"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h3>
<div class="overflow-x-auto"><table class="custom-table"><thead><tr><th>✅ Pros</th><th>❌ Cons</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Easy to implement</td><td>Not scalable</td></tr><tr><td>Minimal setup</td><td>Becomes cluttered as the project grows</td></tr><tr><td>Ideal for small teams or solo developers</td><td>Lack of clear separation of concerns</td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<hr/>
<h2 id="2-atomic-design-scalable-component-organization">2. Atomic Design: Scalable Component Organization<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#2-atomic-design-scalable-component-organization"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h2>
<p><img src="/_astro/diagram.WxVUv673_2noNMU.svg" alt="Atomic Design Diagram" loading="lazy" decoding="async" fetchpriority="auto" width="500" height="100"></p>
<p>For larger Vue applications, Atomic Design provides a clear structure. This approach organizes components into a hierarchy from simplest to most complex.</p>
<h3 id="the-atomic-hierarchy">The Atomic Hierarchy<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#the-atomic-hierarchy"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h3>
<ul>
<li><strong>Atoms:</strong> Basic elements like buttons and icons.</li>
<li><strong>Molecules:</strong> Groups of atoms forming simple components (e.g., search bars).</li>
<li><strong>Organisms:</strong> Complex components made up of molecules and atoms (e.g., navigation bars).</li>
<li><strong>Templates:</strong> Page layouts that structure organisms without real content.</li>
<li><strong>Pages:</strong> Templates filled with real content to form actual pages.</li>
</ul>
<p>This method ensures scalability and maintainability, facilitating a smooth transition between simple and complex components.</p>

<h3 id="pros-and-cons-1">Pros and Cons<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#pros-and-cons-1"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h3>
<div class="overflow-x-auto"><table class="custom-table"><thead><tr><th>✅ Pros</th><th>❌ Cons</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Highly scalable</td><td>Can introduce overhead in managing layers</td></tr><tr><td>Organized component hierarchy</td><td>Initial complexity in setting up</td></tr><tr><td>Reusable components</td><td>Might be overkill for smaller projects</td></tr><tr><td>Improves collaboration among teams</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<aside aria-label="Want to Learn More About Atomic Design?" class="aside aside-info astro-37uy2q7c"> <div class="aside-content astro-37uy2q7c"> <p class="aside-title astro-37uy2q7c"> <span class="aside-emoji astro-37uy2q7c" role="img" aria-hidden="true">ℹ️</span> Want to Learn More About Atomic Design? </p> <section class="aside-body astro-37uy2q7c"> <p>Check out my detailed blog post on <a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="../atomic-design-vue-or-nuxt">Atomic Design in Vue and
Nuxt</a>.</p> </section> </div> </aside> 
<hr/>
<h2 id="3-modular-approach-feature-based-organization">3. Modular Approach: Feature-Based Organization<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#3-modular-approach-feature-based-organization"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h2>
<p>As your project scales, consider a <strong>Modular Monolithic Architecture</strong>. This structure encapsulates each feature or domain, enhancing maintainability and preparing for potential evolution towards microservices.</p>

<h3 id="alternative-simplified-flat-feature-structure">Alternative: Simplified Flat Feature Structure<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#alternative-simplified-flat-feature-structure"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h3>

astro-o25vlg2d">ProjectList.vue</span>  </span> </li> <li class="file-tree__item astro-o25vlg2d" style="--level: 2;">   <span class="file-tree__file astro-o25vlg2d">  <svg class="file-tree__icon astro-o25vlg2d">ProjectItem.vue</span>  </span> </li>  </ul> </details>   </li>  </ul> </details>   </li>  </ul> </nav> 
<p>This structure offers key advantages:</p>
<ul>
<li><strong>Quick Navigation</strong>: Using IDE features like “Quick Open” (Ctrl/Cmd + P), you can find any project-related file by typing “project…”</li>
<li><strong>Reduced Nesting</strong>: All feature-related files are at the same level, eliminating deep folder hierarchies</li>
<li><strong>Clear Ownership</strong>: Each file’s name indicates its purpose</li>
<li><strong>Pattern Recognition</strong>: Consistent naming makes it simple to understand each file’s role</li>
<li><strong>Test Colocation</strong>: Tests live right next to the code they’re testing</li>
</ul>
<hr/>
<h2 id="4-feature-sliced-design-for-complex-applications">4. Feature-Sliced Design: For Complex Applications<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#4-feature-sliced-design-for-complex-applications"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h2>
<p><strong>Feature-Sliced Design</strong> is ideal for big, long-term projects. This approach breaks the application into different layers, each with a specific role.</p>
<p><img src="/_astro/feature-sliced.DQ2OVzxU_Z1C1Cv3.webp" alt="Feature-Sliced Design Diagram" loading="lazy" decoding="async" fetchpriority="auto" width="1730" height="970"></p>
<h3 id="layers-of-feature-sliced-design">Layers of Feature-Sliced Design<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#layers-of-feature-sliced-design"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h3>
<ul>
<li><strong>App:</strong> Global settings, styles, and providers.</li>
<li><strong>Processes:</strong> Global business processes, like user authentication flows.</li>
<li><strong>Pages:</strong> Full pages built using entities, features, and widgets.</li>
<li><strong>Widgets:</strong> Combines entities and features into cohesive UI blocks.</li>
<li><strong>Features:</strong> Handles user interactions that add value.</li>
<li><strong>Entities:</strong> Represents core business models.</li>
<li><strong>Shared:</strong> Reusable utilities and components unrelated to specific business logic.</li>
</ul>

<h3 id="pros-and-cons-2">Pros and Cons<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#pros-and-cons-2"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h3>
<div class="overflow-x-auto"><table class="custom-table"><thead><tr><th>✅ Pros</th><th>❌ Cons</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>High cohesion and clear separation</td><td>Initial complexity in understanding the layers</td></tr><tr><td>Scalable and maintainable</td><td>Requires thorough planning</td></tr><tr><td>Facilitates team collaboration</td><td>Needs consistent enforcement of conventions</td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<aside aria-label="Learn More About Feature-Sliced Design" class="aside aside-tip astro-37uy2q7c"> <div class="aside-content astro-37uy2q7c"> <p class="aside-title astro-37uy2q7c"> <span class="aside-emoji astro-37uy2q7c" role="img" aria-hidden="true">💡</span> Learn More About Feature-Sliced Design </p> <section class="aside-body astro-37uy2q7c"> <p>Visit the <a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://feature-sliced.design/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">official Feature-Sliced Design
documentation</a> for an in-depth understanding.</p> </section> </div> </aside> 
<hr/>
<h2 id="5-micro-frontends-enterprise-level-solution">5. Micro Frontends: Enterprise-Level Solution<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#5-micro-frontends-enterprise-level-solution"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h2>
<p><strong>Micro frontends</strong> apply the microservices concept to frontend development. Teams can work on distinct sections of a web app independently, enabling flexible development and deployment.</p>
<p><img src="/_astro/microfrontend.C9Rblbrg_Z1UojTu.webp" alt="Micro Frontend Diagram" loading="lazy" decoding="async" fetchpriority="auto" width="1730" height="876"></p>
<h3 id="key-components">Key Components<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#key-components"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h3>
<ul>
<li><strong>Application Shell:</strong> The main controller handling basic layout and routing, connecting all micro frontends.</li>
<li><strong>Decomposed UIs:</strong> Each micro frontend focuses on a specific part of the application using its own technology stack.</li>
</ul>
<h3 id="pros-and-cons-3">Pros and Cons<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#pros-and-cons-3"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h3>
<div class="overflow-x-auto"><table class="custom-table"><thead><tr><th>✅ Pros</th><th>❌ Cons</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Independent deployments</td><td>High complexity in orchestration</td></tr><tr><td>Scalability across large teams</td><td>Requires robust infrastructure</td></tr><tr><td>Technology-agnostic approach</td><td>Potential inconsistencies in user experience</td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<aside aria-label="Note" class="aside aside-caution astro-37uy2q7c"> <div class="aside-content astro-37uy2q7c"> <p class="aside-title astro-37uy2q7c"> <span class="aside-emoji astro-37uy2q7c" role="img" aria-hidden="true">⚠️</span> Note </p> <section class="aside-body astro-37uy2q7c"> <p>Micro frontends are best suited for large, complex projects with multiple
development teams. This approach can introduce significant complexity and is
usually not necessary for small to medium-sized applications.</p> </section> </div> </aside> 
<aside aria-label="Deep Dive into Microfrontends" class="aside aside-tip astro-37uy2q7c"> <div class="aside-content astro-37uy2q7c"> <p class="aside-title astro-37uy2q7c"> <span class="aside-emoji astro-37uy2q7c" role="img" aria-hidden="true">💡</span> Deep Dive into Microfrontends </p> <section class="aside-body astro-37uy2q7c"> <p>Want to learn how to actually implement microfrontends with Vue? Check out my
comprehensive guide: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="../how-to-build-microfrontends-with-module-federation-and-vue">How to build Microfrontends with Module Federation and
Vue</a> - includes
working code, architectural decisions, and a complete reference project.</p> </section> </div> </aside> 
<hr/>
<h2 id="conclusion">Conclusion<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#conclusion"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h2>
<p><img src="/_astro/conclusion.CHAaMtv7_Z10ly0U.webp" alt="Conclusion" loading="lazy" decoding="async" fetchpriority="auto" width="1290" height="970"></p>
<p>Selecting the right project structure depends on your project’s size, complexity, and team organization. The more complex your team or project is, the more you should aim for a structure that facilitates scalability and maintainability.</p>
<p>Your project’s architecture should grow with your organization, providing a solid foundation for future development.</p>
<h3 id="comparison-chart">Comparison Chart<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#comparison-chart"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h3>
<div class="overflow-x-auto"><table class="custom-table"><thead><tr><th>Approach</th><th>Description</th><th>✅ Pros</th><th>❌ Cons</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><strong>Flat Structure</strong></td><td>Simple structure for small projects</td><td>Easy to implement</td><td>Not scalable, can become cluttered</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Atomic Design</strong></td><td>Hierarchical component-based structure</td><td>Scalable, organized, reusable components</td><td>Overhead in managing layers, initial complexity</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Modular Approach</strong></td><td>Feature-based modular structure</td><td>Scalable, encapsulated features</td><td>Potential duplication, requires discipline</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Feature-Sliced Design</strong></td><td>Functional layers and slices for large projects</td><td>High cohesion, clear separation</td><td>Initial complexity, requires thorough planning</td></tr><tr><td><strong>Micro Frontends</strong></td><td>Independent deployments of frontend components</td><td>Independent deployments, scalable</td><td>High complexity, requires coordination between teams</td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<hr/>
<h2 id="general-rules-and-best-practices">General Rules and Best Practices<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#general-rules-and-best-practices"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h2>
<p>Before concluding, let’s highlight some general rules you can apply to every structure. These guidelines are important for maintaining consistency and readability in your codebase.</p>
<h3 id="base-component-names">Base Component Names<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#base-component-names"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h3>
<p>Use a prefix for your UI components to distinguish them from other components.</p>
<p><strong>Bad:</strong></p>

<h3 id="related-component-names">Related Component Names<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#related-component-names"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h3>
<p>Group related components together by naming them accordingly.</p>
<p><strong>Bad:</strong></p>

<h3 id="order-of-words-in-component-names">Order of Words in Component Names<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#order-of-words-in-component-names"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h3>

<h3 id="organizing-tests">Organizing Tests<a class="heading-link" aria-label="Link to section" href="#organizing-tests"><span class="heading-link-icon">#</span></a></h3>

      function initInternalLinks() {
        const wrappers = document.querySelectorAll(".internal-link-wrapper");

        wrappers.forEach(wrapper => {
          const card = wrapper.querySelector(".preview-card");
          const link = wrapper.querySelector(".internal-link");
          if (!card || !link) return;

          // Skip if already initialized
          if (wrapper.dataset.initialized === "true") return;
          wrapper.dataset.initialized = "true";

          // Function to hide the card
          const hideCard = () => {
            card.classList.remove("is-fixed");
            card.style.removeProperty("--pc-top");
            card.style.removeProperty("--pc-left");
            card.style.opacity = "";
            card.style.visibility = "";
            // Remove scroll listener when hiding
            window.removeEventListener("scroll", hideCard);
          };

          wrapper.addEventListener("mouseenter", () => {
            // Make visible first so it has size
            card.style.opacity = "1";
            card.style.visibility = "visible";

            // Use fixed positioning to escape overflow clipping
            const linkRect = link.getBoundingClientRect();
            const cardRect = card.getBoundingClientRect();

            // Position above by default; flip below if too close to top
            const aboveTop = linkRect.top - 8 - cardRect.height;
            const belowTop = linkRect.bottom + 8;
            const top = aboveTop < 10 ? belowTop : aboveTop;

            // Center horizontally on the link
            const left = linkRect.left + linkRect.width / 2 - cardRect.width / 2;

            // Constrain to viewport
            const vw = document.documentElement.clientWidth;
            const safeLeft = Math.max(8, Math.min(left, vw - cardRect.width - 8));

            // Apply fixed position with coordinates
            card.classList.add("is-fixed");
            card.style.setProperty("--pc-top", `${Math.round(top)}px`);
            card.style.setProperty("--pc-left", `${Math.round(safeLeft)}px`);

            // Hide card on scroll
            window.addEventListener("scroll", hideCard, { passive: true });
          });

          wrapper.addEventListener("mouseleave", hideCard);
        });
      }

      // Initialize on both initial load and after client-side navigation
      document.addEventListener("astro:page-load", initInternalLinks);
    </script> </body> </html>  <script>(function(){const postSlug = "how-to-structure-vue-projects";

  function updateCTAFollowVisibility() {
    const cta = document.getElementById("cta-follow");
    const article = document.getElementById("article");
    if (!cta || !article) return;

    // If it has the force-hidden class, don't try to show it
    if (cta.classList.contains("force-hidden")) {
      return;
    }

    const viewportHeight = window.innerHeight;
    const articleBottom = article.getBoundingClientRect().bottom;

    // Only show if user has reached the end of the article (article bottom is visible)
    // and hasn't dismissed or subscribed
    if (
      articleBottom <= viewportHeight + 100 && // 100px buffer
      !localStorage.getItem("newsletter_dismissed") &&
      !localStorage.getItem("newsletter_subscribed")
    ) {
      cta.dataset.visible = "true";
      cta.style.transform = "translateX(0)";
      cta.style.opacity = "1";
    } else {
      cta.dataset.visible = "false";
      cta.style.transform = "translateX(-120%)";
      cta.style.opacity = "0";
    }
  }

  // Initialize visibility check
  window.addEventListener("scroll", updateCTAFollowVisibility);
  window.addEventListener("resize", updateCTAFollowVisibility);

  // Add a small delay to initial check to ensure proper positioning
  setTimeout(updateCTAFollowVisibility, 500);

  // Handle newsletter subscribe click with proper tracking
  document
    .getElementById("newsletter-subscribe-button")
    ?.addEventListener("click", () => {
      localStorage.setItem("newsletter_subscribed", "true");

      // Force the popup to stay hidden
      const cta = document.getElementById("cta-follow");
      if (cta) {
        cta.classList.add("force-hidden");
        cta.style.transform = "translateX(-120%)";
        cta.style.opacity = "0";
      }

      if (window.plausible) {
        window.plausible("Newsletter Subscribe Click", {
          props: {
            post: postSlug,
            location: "end_of_article",
            source: "notification",
          },
        });
      }
    });

  // Handle newsletter dismiss click
  document
    .getElementById("newsletter-dismiss")
    ?.addEventListener("click", function () {
      const slug = this.getAttribute("data-post-slug");
      localStorage.setItem("newsletter_dismissed", "true");

      const cta = document.getElementById("cta-follow");
      if (cta) {
        cta.classList.add("force-hidden");
        cta.style.transform = "translateX(-120%)";
        cta.style.opacity = "0";
      }

      if (window.plausible) {
        window.plausible("Newsletter Dismissed", {
          props: {
            post: slug,
            location: "end_of_article",
            source: "notification",
          },
        });
      }
    });
})();</script>  <script>
  /** Create a progress indicator
   *  at the top */
  function createProgressBar() {
    // Create the main container div
    const progressContainer = document.createElement("div");
    progressContainer.className =
      "progress-container fixed top-0 z-10 h-1 w-full bg-skin-fill";

    // Create the progress bar div
    const progressBar = document.createElement("div");
    progressBar.className = "progress-bar h-1 w-0 bg-skin-accent";
    progressBar.id = "myBar";

    // Append the progress bar to the progress container
    progressContainer.appendChild(progressBar);

    // Append the progress container to the document body or any other desired parent element
    document.body.appendChild(progressContainer);
  }
  createProgressBar();

  /** Update the progress bar
   *  when user scrolls */
  function updateScrollProgress() {
    const winScroll =
      document.body.scrollTop || document.documentElement.scrollTop;
    const height =
      document.documentElement.scrollHeight -
      document.documentElement.clientHeight;
    const scrolled = (winScroll / height) * 100;
    const myBar = document.getElementById("myBar");
    if (myBar) {
      myBar.style.width = scrolled + "%";
    }
  }
  document.addEventListener("scroll", updateScrollProgress);

  /** Make headings groups for hover effect on anchor links */
  function makeHeadingsGroups() {
    const headings = Array.from(
      document.querySelectorAll(".prose h2, .prose h3, .prose h4, .prose h5, .prose h6")
    );
    for (const heading of headings) {
      heading.classList.add("group");
    }
  }

  // Run after DOM is loaded
  if (document.readyState === "loading") {
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", makeHeadingsGroups);
  } else {
    makeHeadingsGroups();
  }

  /** Scroll back to top functionality */
  function attachBackToTop() {
    const backToTopBtn = document.getElementById("back-to-top");
    if (backToTopBtn) {
      backToTopBtn.addEventListener("click", () => {
        window.scrollTo({ top: 0, behavior: "smooth" });
      });
    }
  }
  attachBackToTop();
</script>
